## *Star Wars Rebels*

## Production information

### Format

[Animated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animation "wikipedia:Animation")[[1]](#cite_note-New_Animated_Series-1)

### Episode count

74

### No. of seasons

4

### Run time

* Approx. 22 minutes per episode (30-minute time slot)[[2]](#cite_note-Weisman_on_IGN-2)
* 30 hours 25 minutes  
  (1825 minutes) (total)

### Network(s)

* [Disney Channel](/wiki/Disney_Channel "Disney Channel") ([film](/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels:_Spark_of_Rebellion "Star Wars Rebels: Spark of Rebellion") premiere)[[1]](#cite_note-New_Animated_Series-1)
* [Disney XD](/wiki/Disney_XD "Disney XD")[[1]](#cite_note-New_Animated_Series-1)

### First aired

* [October 3](/wiki/October_3 "October 3"), [2014](/wiki/2014 "2014")[[3]](#cite_note-Premiere-3) (film premiere)

## Chronological information

### Timeline

* [5 BBY](/wiki/5_BBY "5 BBY") - [1 BBY](/wiki/1_BBY "1 BBY")[[23]](#cite_note-Date-23)
* c. [9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY") (Epilogue)[[23]](#cite_note-Date-23)

[[Source]](https://starwars.fandom.com/wiki/Template:TelevisionSeries)

:   "Star Wars Rebels *is an adventure show that focuses on a street-smart teenage boy who just might have what it takes to be a Jedi, and who joins a small band of rebels that engages in daring missions of resistance against the evil Galactic Empire.*"
:   ―[Rayne Roberts](/wiki/Rayne_Roberts "Rayne Roberts"), [*Star Wars Insider* 152](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_152 "Star Wars Insider 152")[[24]](#cite_note-Rebel_Friends!-24)

***Star Wars Rebels*** is an animated television series set during the [time](/wiki/Time "Time") frame between the films [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith") and [*Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope"). It premiered worldwide as a one-hour television movie, *[Star Wars Rebels: Spark of Rebellion](/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels:_Spark_of_Rebellion "Star Wars Rebels: Spark of Rebellion")*, on [Disney Channel](/wiki/Disney_Channel "Disney Channel") on [October 3](/wiki/October_3 "October 3"), [2014](/wiki/2014 "2014"); Regular episodes aired for four seasons on [Disney XD](/wiki/Disney_XD "Disney XD"), from [October 13](/wiki/October_13 "October 13"), 2014 to [March 5](/wiki/March_5 "March 5"), [2018](/wiki/2018 "2018"). During its run, the series was nominated for four [Emmy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmy_Awards "wikipedia:Emmy Awards"), including two consecutive nominations for "Outstanding Children's Program."[[25]](#cite_note-25)

The series follows a motley group of [rebels](/wiki/Spectres "Spectres") who live aboard the [starship](/wiki/VCX-100_light_freighter "VCX-100 light freighter") *[Ghost](/wiki/Ghost "Ghost")* as they [fight](/wiki/Early_rebellion_against_the_Galactic_Empire "Early rebellion against the Galactic Empire") the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire"). The rebels include [Ezra Bridger](/wiki/Ezra_Bridger "Ezra Bridger"), a young orphan from [Lothal](/wiki/Lothal "Lothal") who learns he can use [the Force](/wiki/The_Force "The Force"); [Kanan Jarrus](/wiki/Kanan_Jarrus "Kanan Jarrus"), a [Jedi](/wiki/Jedi "Jedi") who survived [Order 66](/wiki/Order_66 "Order 66"); [Hera Syndulla](/wiki/Hera_Syndulla "Hera Syndulla"), a [Twi'lek](/wiki/Twi%27lek "Twi'lek") [pilot](/wiki/Pilot "Pilot") and veteran resistance fighter; [Sabine Wren](/wiki/Sabine_Wren "Sabine Wren"), a [Mandalorian](/wiki/Mandalore "Mandalore") explosives expert; [Garazeb "Zeb" Orrelios](/wiki/Garazeb_Orrelios "Garazeb Orrelios"), a [Lasat](/wiki/Lasat "Lasat") warrior; and the cantankerous [astromech droid](/wiki/Astromech_droid "Astromech droid") [C1-10P](/wiki/C1-10P "C1-10P"), also known as Chopper. The crew will eventually help give rise to the [Rebel Alliance](/wiki/Alliance_to_Restore_the_Republic "Alliance to Restore the Republic").

Lucasfilm first announced *Star Wars Rebels* on [May 20](/wiki/May_20 "May 20"), [2013](/wiki/2013 "2013"), following the news that the animated television series *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* would be ending and that a new series would be produced. *Star Wars Rebels* was the first new major *Star Wars* project to be released following [The Walt Disney Company](/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company "The Walt Disney Company")'s acquisition of [Lucasfilm](/wiki/Lucasfilm "Lucasfilm") in [2012](/wiki/2012 "2012"). The series was created by [Dave Filoni](/wiki/Dave_Filoni "Dave Filoni"), [Simon Kinberg](/wiki/Simon_Kinberg "Simon Kinberg"), and [Carrie Beck](/wiki/Carrie_Beck "Carrie Beck"), and stars actors [Taylor Gray](/wiki/Taylor_Gray "Taylor Gray"), [Freddie Prinze Jr.](/wiki/Freddie_Prinze_Jr. "Freddie Prinze Jr."), [Vanessa Marshall](/wiki/Vanessa_Marshall "Vanessa Marshall"), [Tiya Sircar](/wiki/Tiya_Sircar "Tiya Sircar"), [Steve Blum](/wiki/Steve_Blum "Steve Blum"), and Dave Filoni.

## Plot summary[]

### Premise[]

:   "*…we're going to really show the origins of the rebellion. When our series begins, it's not the Rebel Alliance yet; we start with a group of rebels. It'll be really interesting to show the progress of the Alliance forming…*"
:   ―Executive producer Greg Weisman, *Star Wars Insider* 146[[26]](#cite_note-Insider_146:_Weisman_Interview-26)

The series begins five years before [*Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope"), fourteen [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") into the [reign](/wiki/Imperial_Era "Imperial Era") of the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire").[[27]](#cite_note-NYCC_2013_Recap-27)[[28]](#cite_note-Hidalgo_on_Twitter-28) The general premise is described as follows:
"It is a dark time in [the galaxy](/wiki/The_galaxy "The galaxy"), as the evil Galactic Empire tightens its grip of power from [world](/wiki/Planet "Planet") to world. As the series begins, Imperial forces have occupied a [remote planet](/wiki/Lothal "Lothal"), ruling with an iron fist and ruining the lives of its people. But there are a select few who are brave enough to stand up against the endless [Stormtroopers](/wiki/Stormtrooper "Stormtrooper") and [TIE fighters](/wiki/TIE/ln_space_superiority_starfighter "TIE/ln space superiority starfighter") of the Empire: the clever and motley crew of the [starship](/wiki/Starship "Starship") *[Ghost](/wiki/Ghost "Ghost")*. Together, this ragtag group will face threatening new villains, have thrilling adventures, and become heroes."[[29]](#cite_note-Rebels_Packing_Revealed-29)

## Development[]

### Conception[]

:   "*They wanted to do an animated show and I loved [Cartoon Network's] Clone Wars and grew up with a lot of animated shows. So we just started to talk about where it would fall in the general Star Wars timeline. Really there was no predetermination going in. It could have been a prequel, sequel, a stand-alone universe.*"
:   ―Simon Kinberg[[30]](#cite_note-Kinberg-30)

*Star Wars Rebels* was created by [Dave Filoni](/wiki/Dave_Filoni "Dave Filoni"), [Simon Kinberg](/wiki/Simon_Kinberg "Simon Kinberg"), and [Carrie Beck](/wiki/Carrie_Beck "Carrie Beck").[[3]](#cite_note-Premiere-3) The concept originated with Beck, who suggested it be about "this [A-team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_A-Team "wikipedia:The A-Team") group that went around righting wrongs." This reminded Filoni of his original concept for *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")*,[[31]](#cite_note-31) which he described in *[The Art of Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/The_Art_of_Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "The Art of Star Wars: The Clone Wars")*: "My rough idea was to deal with a small number of characters [a Jedi Master and Padawan, a smuggler and his girlfriend, and a [Gungan](/wiki/Gungan "Gungan") "strongman" called Lunker], have them based on a *[Millennium Falcon](/wiki/Millennium_Falcon "Millennium Falcon")*-style smuggling ship, and involve them in black market trade, war espionage, and other stories that existed outside the giant galactic conflict going on in the background."[[32]](#cite_note-The_Art_of_Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars-32)

Discussion of where *Rebels* would fall in the *Star Wars* timeline led to the decision to center the series on the Rebel Alliance. Thus, the series was placed between [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith") and *Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*, during the reign of the Galactic Empire, though not so close to *A New Hope* that it would feel repetitive.[[30]](#cite_note-Kinberg-30) In contrast to the galaxy-hopping structure of *The Clone Wars*, it was decided *Rebels* would depict the Rebellion from one group of characters' point of view. According to Filoni, Kinberg likened it to imagining a show set during the [American Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "wikipedia:American Revolution") "that was about five guys that were locked up in a farmhouse somewhere fighting against the local British military and without any real knowledge of the larger political movements." He also noted how the [original trilogy](/wiki/Original_trilogy "Original trilogy") mentioned events like the dissolution of the [Imperial Senate](/wiki/Imperial_Senate "Imperial Senate") without depicting them.[[33]](#cite_note-33)

The development team set out to differentiate the series from *The Clone Wars* by basing much of the visuals on the designs of [Ralph McQuarrie](/wiki/Ralph_McQuarrie "Ralph McQuarrie")—the artist who developed concept art for much of the original trilogy of films.[[30]](#cite_note-Kinberg-30) *Rebels* was influenced by ideas developed by [George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas") for *[Star Wars: Underworld](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Underworld "Star Wars: Underworld")*,[[34]](#cite_note-34) and much of the action in *Rebels* was influenced by the *[Indiana Jones](/wiki/Indiana_Jones "Indiana Jones")* franchise which George Lucas also contributed to.[[35]](#cite_note-35) Early in development, Disney wanted a more comedy-oriented series than Lucasfilm was interested in making. Kathleen Kennedy and the *Rebels* creative team had to make their case otherwise.[[36]](#cite_note-36) At one point, Filoni considered involving the [Death Star plans](/wiki/Death_Star_plans "Death Star plans") in the show, but abandoned the idea after [*Rogue One*](/wiki/Rogue_One:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Rogue One: A Star Wars Story") began development.[[37]](#cite_note-37) He later planned to have appearances from the [Death Star](/wiki/Death_Star "Death Star") and [Orson Krennic](/wiki/Orson_Callan_Krennic "Orson Callan Krennic"), but decided it was best to focus on things that directly affect the *Ghost* crew.[[38]](#cite_note-38)

### Production[]

:   "*It has been great seeing the mind meld between our executive producers Dave Filoni, Simon Kinberg, and Greg Weisman during the writers' conferences. [...] Everyone on the team is so passionate about* Rebels*, and of course it helps that we are all huge fans of* Star Wars*!*"
:   ―Athena Portillo, *Star Wars Insider* 146[[8]](#cite_note-Insider_152:_Launch_Pad-8)

 [![Ralph McQuarrie&ndash;inspired concept art of the starship Ghost, chased by TIE fighters.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/53/GhostImperialConvoyRaidConcept.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20240404133803) [![Ralph McQuarrie&ndash;inspired concept art of the starship Ghost, chased by TIE fighters.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/53/GhostImperialConvoyRaidConcept.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/275?cb=20240404133803)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/53/GhostImperialConvoyRaidConcept.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20240404133803) 

Ralph McQuarrie–inspired concept art of the starship *Ghost*, chased by TIE fighters.

 

[Lucasfilm](/wiki/Lucasfilm "Lucasfilm") veteran sculptor [Darren Marshall](/wiki/Darren_Marshall "Darren Marshall"), who worked on *Star Wars: The Clone Wars* prior to its cancellation, developed sculpts for the core characters of *Star Wars Rebels* before leaving Lucasfilm in [June](/wiki/June "June") [2013](/wiki/2013 "2013").[[39]](#cite_note-Sculpting_TCW-39) By [December](/wiki/December "December") 2013, the production crew had finished developing the series' [first season](/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels_Season_One "Star Wars Rebels Season One") and had begun animating the first script.[[40]](#cite_note-Insider_146:_Launch_Pad-40) As of January 2014, the scripts for Season One were halfway completed. Voice-recording had been finished for five episodes, with three more episodes undergoing storyboarding, two more undergoing animation, and the first episode undergoing lighting. Sound design was also underway, with a theme in place for the series.[[41]](#cite_note-Insider_147:_Launch_Pad-41) [Greg Weisman](/wiki/Greg_Weisman "Greg Weisman") joined the project as an executive producer in [May](/wiki/May "May") 2013, though the series had been under development well before then.[[42]](#cite_note-Scum-42)

On [January 17](/wiki/January_17 "January 17"), animation supervisor [Keith Kellogg](/wiki/Keith_Kellogg "Keith Kellogg") announced that the production crew had wrapped up animation on the first episode of the series.[[43]](#cite_note-Kellogg_on_Twitter-43) To aid in animating the show, Lucasfilm developed a special tool for [Adobe Photoshop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adobe_Photoshop "wikipedia:Adobe Photoshop") that emulates Ralph McQuarrie's artistic style;[[44]](#cite_note-lucasfilm.com-44) the character Zeb Orrelios is based on McQuarie's original concept art for the [Wookiee](/wiki/Wookiee "Wookiee") [Chewbacca](/wiki/Chewbacca "Chewbacca").[[22]](#cite_note-Meet_Zeb-22) The series' look is also inspired by the work of [Hayao Miyazaki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hayao_Miyazaki "wikipedia:Hayao Miyazaki")—a favorite of Lucasfilm President [Kathleen Kennedy](/wiki/Kathleen_Kennedy "Kathleen Kennedy").[[45]](#cite_note-'Star_Wars_Rebels':_Dave_Filoni_takes_'Star_Wars'_back_to_its_roots-45) Filoni requested that the animation crew look at the Disney film [*Tangled*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tangled "wikipedia:Tangled"), for which 2D facial expressions were created using 3D animation.[[46]](#cite_note-46) Simon Kinberg wrote the series' first two episodes, which serve as a short story arc to introduce the show's main characters.[[30]](#cite_note-Kinberg-30) By [March](/wiki/March "March") 2014, the entire first season had been mapped out, and according to Greg Weisman, the series as a whole is organized as a three-act play. The first season serves as the first act of the overall series, while the second and third acts may take more than one season.[[42]](#cite_note-Scum-42)

*Star Wars Rebels* was overseen by three executive producers: Dave Filoni, Simon Kinberg, and Greg Weisman.[[47]](#cite_note-Insider_143:_Launch_Pad-47) In addition to Filoni, the *Rebels* production team included several crew members returning from *Star Wars: The Clone Wars*: [Athena Yvette Portillo](/wiki/Athena_Yvette_Portillo "Athena Yvette Portillo") as line producer, [Kilian Plunkett](/wiki/Kilian_Plunkett "Kilian Plunkett") as art director, [Joel Aron](/wiki/Joel_Aron "Joel Aron") as CG effects supervisor, Keith Kellogg as animation supervisor, and [Steward Lee](/wiki/Steward_Lee "Steward Lee") as episodic director. Lee, Filoni's longest-running episodic director from *The Clone Wars*, was joined in directorial duties by brother [Steven G. Lee](/wiki/Steven_G._Lee "Steven G. Lee"), a veteran of [LucasArts](/wiki/LucasArts "LucasArts").[[27]](#cite_note-NYCC_2013_Recap-27) [Kevin Kiner](/wiki/Kevin_Kiner "Kevin Kiner"), who was previously the composer for *Star Wars: The Clone Wars*, returned as the new music composer for *Star Wars Rebels*.[[48]](#cite_note-WonderCon_Blog-48) Lucasfilm hired music producer [Flux Pavillion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flux_Pavillion "wikipedia:Flux Pavillion") to remix Kiner's *Rebels* main theme.[[49]](#cite_note-49) Other returning crew members from *The Clone Wars* included [Amy Beth Christenson](/wiki/Amy_Beth_Christenson "Amy Beth Christenson"), [Andre Kirk](/wiki/Andre_Kirk "Andre Kirk"), [Pat Presley](/wiki/Pat_Presley "Pat Presley"), and [Chris Glenn](/wiki/Chris_Glenn "Chris Glenn") on the concept art team, managed by [Liz Cummings](/wiki/Liz_Cummings "Liz Cummings"), as well as [Paul Zinnes](/wiki/Paul_Zinnes "Paul Zinnes") on the development team.[[47]](#cite_note-Insider_143:_Launch_Pad-47) [Pablo Hidalgo](/wiki/Pablo_Hidalgo "Pablo Hidalgo"), a member of the [Lucasfilm Story Group](/wiki/Lucasfilm_Story_Group "Lucasfilm Story Group"), also worked with the team as a fact-checker.[[27]](#cite_note-NYCC_2013_Recap-27)[[26]](#cite_note-Insider_146:_Weisman_Interview-26) The crew aimed for an overall aesthetic similar to the original trilogy. As such, Joel Aron tried to give the visuals a "grainy look," Matthew Wood used many of the original trilogy's sound effects for the series' soundtrack,[[50]](#cite_note-50) and the crew animated the lightsabers in such a way as to emulate the look of those in the original trilogy.[[51]](#cite_note-51)

## Release and reception[]

 [![Imperial propaganda poster created to promote the series](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/70/Rebelspropaganda.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20140205170306) [![Imperial propaganda poster created to promote the series](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/70/Rebelspropaganda.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20140205170306)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/70/Rebelspropaganda.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20140205170306) 

Imperial propaganda poster created to promote the series

 

:   "*Citizens of Lothal: It is by Imperial Decree that you are requested to proudly display these posters on behalf of your Empire. As loyal residents of one of the Empire's most vital stations on the Outer Rim, your compliance is appreciated. Imperial Service is a noble endeavor which paves the way for your freedom and security. Remember, it is the will of Emperor Palpatine to ensure the future of a stable and prosperous galaxy.*"
:   ―Letter included in the *Star Wars Rebels* propaganda poster mailing promotion[[52]](#cite_note-Twitter-CanadianFanboy-52)

*Star Wars Rebels* was first announced on [March 11](/wiki/March_11 "March 11"), 2013, as an unnamed animated series set to replace *Star Wars: The Clone Wars*.[[53]](#cite_note-New_Direction-53) Its name and fall 2014 premiere were announced in a press release on [May 20](/wiki/May_20 "May 20"), 2013.[[1]](#cite_note-New_Animated_Series-1) The first [*Star Wars Rebels* teaser trailer](http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=O1_F7zg4B30) debuted on the [*Star Wars* YouTube channel](https://www.youtube.com/user/starwars) on [October 7](/wiki/October_7 "October 7"), 2013.[[54]](#cite_note-Rebels_Teaser_Trailer-54) The series' main characters were first revealed at the [January](/wiki/January "January") [2014](/wiki/2014 "2014") [Nuremberg International Toy Fair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuremberg_International_Toy_Fair "wikipedia:Nuremberg International Toy Fair"), which showcased forthcoming *[LEGO Star Wars Rebels](/wiki/LEGO_Star_Wars_Rebels "LEGO Star Wars Rebels")* sets. The sets, which depict the *Ghost* and the attack shuttle *[Phantom](/wiki/Phantom "Phantom")*, included minifigures for Ezra Bridger, Zeb Orrelios, Hera Syndulla, and a placeholder for Kanan Jarrus.[[55]](#cite_note-Groove_Bricks-55) The box originally identified Zeb's last name as "Orretios,"[[56]](#cite_note-Jedi_News:_LEGO_Minifigs-56) but the finalized boxes at the New York Toy Fair not long afterward corrected the name and included Jarrus' minifigure.[[57]](#cite_note-Toy_Fair_Hasbro-57)

On [February 4](/wiki/February_4 "February 4"), 2014, Lucasfilm distributed six original artwork pieces by Amy Beth Christenson exclusively to six select websites across the Internet—[*Empire*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine) "wikipedia:Empire (film magazine)"),[[58]](#cite_note-Propaganda_Posters_Empire-58) [*ET Online*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entertainment_Tonight "wikipedia:Entertainment Tonight"),[[59]](#cite_note-Propaganda_Posters_ET-59) [*IGN*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IGN "wikipedia:IGN"),[[60]](#cite_note-Propaganda_Posters_IGN-60) [Mashable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashable "wikipedia:Mashable"),[[61]](#cite_note-Propaganda_Posters_Mashable-61) [Omelete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omelete "wikipedia:Omelete")[[62]](#cite_note-Propaganda_Posters_Omelete-62) and [TheForce.net](/wiki/TheForce.net "TheForce.net")[[63]](#cite_note-Propaganda_Posters_TFN-63)—to promote *Star Wars Rebels*. The artwork, presented in the form of Imperial [propaganda](/wiki/Propaganda "Propaganda") posters, was part of an exclusive mailing campaign, in which limited-edition cards featuring the artwork were sent to 2,500 people around the world on [February 5](/wiki/February_5 "February 5").[[64]](#cite_note-Rebels_Imperial_Propaganda_Posters-64) The mailings arrived in black-embossed envelopes addressed from the [Commission for the Preservation of the New Order](/wiki/Commission_for_the_Preservation_of_the_New_Order "Commission for the Preservation of the New Order") on [Coruscant](/wiki/Coruscant "Coruscant")[[65]](#cite_note-Propaganda_Mailing-65) and included a letter urging citizens to proudly display the posters in support of the Imperial occupation of Lothal.[[52]](#cite_note-Twitter-CanadianFanboy-52) The six card backs, when combined together, formed the *Rebels* phoenix logo.[[66]](#cite_note-Twitter-RebelsReport-66)

Starting with Chopper, the "grumpy astromech droid" on [January 28](/wiki/January_28 "January 28"),[[67]](#cite_note-Star_Wars_Rebels:_Meet_Chopper-67) a series of videos was released that introduced each of the crew members of the *Ghost*. Kanan was introduced as "the Cowboy Jedi" on [February 12](/wiki/February_12 "February 12"),[[19]](#cite_note-Meet_Kanan-19) and "the Street-Smart Hero" Ezra Bridger followed on [February 14](/wiki/February_14 "February 14").[[18]](#cite_note-Meet_Ezra-18) Two *Rebels* teasers, entitled "Spark" and "Ignite," were released on [February 17](/wiki/February_17 "February 17"),[[68]](#cite_note-Spark_teaser-68)[[69]](#cite_note-Ignite-69) and videos introducing Garazeb Orrelios, "the Muscle," Sabine Wren, "the Explosive Artist," and Hera Syndulla, "the Pilot," were released on [February 18](/wiki/February_18 "February 18"),[[22]](#cite_note-Meet_Zeb-22) [19](/wiki/February_19 "February 19"),[[21]](#cite_note-Meet_Sabine-21) and [20](/wiki/February_20 "February 20") respectively.[[20]](#cite_note-Meet_Hera-20) The videos were released by independent news sources such as *TV Guide*, IGN, and *Entertainment Weekly*, and then were posted on the official *Star Wars* YouTube channel shortly afterwards.[[70]](#cite_note-Ezra_TV_Guide-70) On [April 16](/wiki/April_16 "April 16"), in conjunction with a following panel at [WonderCon 2014](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WonderCon "wikipedia:WonderCon"), a clip featuring the character Hera Syndulla was released on the *Star Wars* YouTube channel.[[48]](#cite_note-WonderCon_Blog-48)

 [![Star Wars Rebels movie-style poster, released in advance of San Diego Comic-Con 2014](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/RebelsPoster.png/revision/latest?cb=20140805200015) [![Star Wars Rebels movie-style poster, released in advance of San Diego Comic-Con 2014](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/RebelsPoster.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20140805200015)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/RebelsPoster.png/revision/latest?cb=20140805200015) 

*Star Wars Rebels* movie-style poster, released in advance of San Diego Comic-Con 2014

 

The first full-length trailer for *Rebels* was released on May 4, 2014. A thirty-second preview of the trailer aired on May 2 on [Good Morning America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Morning_America "wikipedia:Good Morning America"), followed by the full trailer on May 4, which aired throughout the day on various Disney networks and became available online at StarWars.com and Disney.com.[[71]](#cite_note-Trailer_Debut-71) On July 9, 2014, [ESPN's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESPN "wikipedia:ESPN") *Wednesday Night Baseball* game between the [St. Louis Cardinals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals "wikipedia:St. Louis Cardinals") and the [Pittsburgh Pirates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates "wikipedia:Pittsburgh Pirates") featured a *Star Wars* theme, including elements from *Star Wars Rebels*.[[72]](#cite_note-'Star_Wars'_Goes_Out_to_the_Ballpark_With_ESPN's_'Wednesday_Night_Baseball'-72) On July 24, 2014, Lucasfilm hosted a panel at the 2014 [San Diego Comic-Con](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International "wikipedia:San Diego Comic-Con International"). Known as "The Heroes of *Star Wars Rebels*," the panel featured Dave Filoni, Simon Kinberg, and the series' principal voice cast.[[73]](#cite_note-''Star_Wars_Rebels''_and_More_at_San_Diego_Comic-Con_2014!-73) Attendees were each given "HoloNet registration cards" that directed them to a re-launched version of [HoloNetNews.com](/wiki/HoloNet_News_(original_website) "HoloNet News (original website)") that features videos of Imperial propaganda.[[74]](#cite_note-TFN_SDCC_2014-74) Around this time, several more promotional videos were released, including two more full-length trailers,[[75]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Star_Wars_Rebels_Extended_Trailer_Official-75)[[76]](#cite_note-Look_Ahead-76) two previews exclusive to San Diego Comic-Con,[[77]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-We're_Even_-_Fighter_Flight_SDCC_2014_Exclusive_Clip_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-77)[[78]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Kanan_vs._The_Inquisitor_-_SDCC_2014_Exclusive_Clip_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-78) as well as videos that introduced [Imperial Security Bureau](/wiki/Imperial_Security_Bureau "Imperial Security Bureau") Agent [Kallus](/wiki/Alexsandr_Kallus "Alexsandr Kallus") and The Inquisitor.[[79]](#cite_note-Meet_Kallus-79)[[80]](#cite_note-Meet_Inquisitor-80) August saw the release of a seven-minute preview,[[81]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Star_Wars_Rebels_Extended_Preview_Official-81) a four-minute preview,[[82]](#cite_note-82) as well as three television spots.[[83]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Tough_Guy_-_TV_Spot_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-83)[[84]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-A_Small_Band_-_TV_Spot_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-84)[[85]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Something_Big_-_TV_Spot_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-85) Beginning on August 11, four three-minute prelude shorts were released consecutively (on a weekly basis) on [Disney XD](/wiki/Disney_XD "Disney XD").[[86]](#cite_note-IGN_Article-86) In September, six more TV spots and another trailer were released.[[87]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Tyranny_of_the_Empire_–_TV_Spot_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-87)[[88]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Timeline_-_TV_Spot_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-88)[[89]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Take_a_Stand_-_TV_Spot_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-89)[[90]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Star_Wars_Rebels:_Join_the_Team_TV_Spot-90)[[91]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Star_Wars_Rebels:_Generations_Trailer-91)[[92]](#cite_note-92)[[93]](#cite_note-93) Also that month, the [Toys "R" Us](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toys_%22R%22_Us "wikipedia:Toys \"R\" Us") website began releasing a series of promotional videos called "Secrets of the Star Wars Rebels" that will run through October.[[94]](#cite_note-94)

On October 2, 2014, Disney announced that it had renewed *Star Wars Rebels* for a second season.[[17]](#cite_note-Season_2_renewal-17) The series debuted the next day on the Disney Channel with the TV movie *[Star Wars Rebels: Spark of Rebellion](/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels:_Spark_of_Rebellion "Star Wars Rebels: Spark of Rebellion")*.[[3]](#cite_note-Premiere-3) Two final TV spots were released prior to the debut of regular episodes on Disney XD on [October 13](/wiki/October_13 "October 13").[[95]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Star_Wars_Rebels:_A_New_Battle_TV_Spot-95)[[96]](#cite_note-SWYouTube-Join_Hera_and_Sabine_-_TV_Spot_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-96)[[1]](#cite_note-New_Animated_Series-1)

All four seasons of the series are available on the [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+") streaming service, which launched on November 12, 2019.[[97]](#cite_note-Disney+-97)

## Continuity[]

:   "*We're all very dedicated, and we know this show is going to be canon, so we take that responsibility very seriously. We know that on the one hand there's an audience who's going to be watching this that knows everything there is to know about Lucasfilm canon and knows beyond that tons of stuff from the Expanded Universe, which may or may not turn out to be canon once Lucasfilm decides what is official and what's not. So we want the show to work for that group, the most extreme fanboys out there. At the same time, we also have the responsibility that for a certain generation of kids, this is going to be their first exposure to Star Wars.*"
:   ―Greg Weisman[[2]](#cite_note-Weisman_on_IGN-2)

Lucasfilm's Pablo Hidalgo first provided a timeline for *Star Wars Rebels* of approximately fourteen years after the events of *Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*, which corresponds to around five years before the events of *Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*.[[27]](#cite_note-NYCC_2013_Recap-27) Although the official [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") press release announcing the *Rebels* character Chopper later alternatively stated a timeline of four years prior to the events of *A New Hope*,[[67]](#cite_note-Star_Wars_Rebels:_Meet_Chopper-67) Hidalgo quickly reaffirmed the original timeframe via Twitter.[[28]](#cite_note-Hidalgo_on_Twitter-28) In reprinting portions of the original StarWars.com Chopper press release, the [*Launch Pad*](/wiki/Launchpad "Launchpad") department from [*Star Wars Insider* 148](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_148 "Star Wars Insider 148") also stated a series timeline of 4 BBY.[[98]](#cite_note-Insider_148:_Launch_Pad-98) Simon Kinberg told *Empire* magazine that the series would have strong connections to the overall saga: "[I've] always felt [*Star Wars Rebels*] would lead into IV and potentially set up characters you might not meet until V, or VI, or even VII, but the notion was that this would stand alone from Episode VII. That doesn't mean that we can't introduce [Easter eggs](/wiki/Easter_egg_(virtual) "Easter egg (virtual)") that will pay off in VII, VIII, IX."[[99]](#cite_note-99)

Dave Filoni originally claimed that Zeb Orrelios was of a new species based on Ralph McQuarrie's concept art for the Wookiee Chewbacca,[[22]](#cite_note-Meet_Zeb-22) but a preexisting [Expanded Universe](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends") species known as the Lasat had already been based on the concept art.[[100]](#cite_note-Back_from_the_Drawing_Board-100) *Star Wars Insider* 148 identified Orrelios as a Lasat, though it misspelled his last name as "Orrelious."[[98]](#cite_note-Insider_148:_Launch_Pad-98) [*Star Wars Insider* 149](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_149 "Star Wars Insider 149") issued an editorial apology for the misspelling but nonetheless misspelled the character's name again, this time as "Orrilios."[[101]](#cite_note-Insider_149:_Launch_Pad-101)

[John Jackson Miller](/wiki/John_Jackson_Miller "John Jackson Miller")'s novel [*A New Dawn*](/wiki/A_New_Dawn_(novel) "A New Dawn (novel)"), which serves as a prequel to *Star Wars Rebels*, is said to be the first narrative to be part of Lucasfilm's Story Group.[[102]](#cite_note-JJM-102)

:   "*The series takes place between Episodes III and IV. By this time, Order 66 has been executed and the Empire's search for the last of the Jedi Knights is in full effect. The events seen in the show take place closer to* A New Hope *in the* Star Wars *timeline. However, if you stay tuned, you may be in for some surprises…*"
:   ―Athena Portillo, *Star Wars Insider* 146[[8]](#cite_note-Insider_152:_Launch_Pad-8)
